        });

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer618900071">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13991072737016842967"> A big resort has been built on Pear Island, aka Breakfast Island, aka Grand Island and Qwill for one is not happy about the changes. Qwill's friends Nick and Lori Bamba are now on the island running a B&amp;B. Nick contacts Qwill because he's concerned about a series of recent accidents and wonders if Qwill would be willing to come over and snoop around. He goes - under the guise of reporting about the island and the resort for the Newspaper - and, of course, life is not dull during his 2 week</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13991072737016842967"> A big resort has been built on Pear Island, aka Breakfast Island, aka Grand Island and Qwill for one is not happy about the changes. Qwill's friends Nick and Lori Bamba are now on the island running a B&amp;B. Nick contacts Qwill because he's concerned about a series of recent accidents and wonders if Qwill would be willing to come over and snoop around. He goes - under the guise of reporting about the island and the resort for the Newspaper - and, of course, life is not dull during his 2 week "vacation".<br /> While I enjoy the lightness of this series, this one seemed lighter and looser to me than some others. Without giving anything away, I feel as if several parts were a real stretch and a manufactured conclusion. There is enough going on with the recurring characters, however, to leave plenty open for the other books of the series.<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer138772853">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11757478618281952515">Ok, so I picked this up partly because I'm in charge of the Mystery/Adventure/Suspense area of my library and it behooves me to know more about the books in that section.<br /><br />But also because there's this parody book called "The Cat Who Killed Lillian Jackson Braun," which I wanted to read. And I felt like I should read one of the books being parodied before I read the funny book.<br /><br />I wasn't thrilled with this little mystery, though I guess I could see what people who DO like these books see in them. Ol</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11757478618281952515">Ok, so I picked this up partly because I'm in charge of the Mystery/Adventure/Suspense area of my library and it behooves me to know more about the books in that section.<br /><br />But also because there's this parody book called "The Cat Who Killed Lillian Jackson Braun," which I wanted to read. And I felt like I should read one of the books being parodied before I read the funny book.<br /><br />I wasn't thrilled with this little mystery, though I guess I could see what people who DO like these books see in them. Older protagonist who is cantankerous and judgmental, talks to his psychic cat, and is wealthy. I like books with smart detectives because it makes me feel smart to be on their side. People like books with this detective because they like to look down on everyone else and bitch and moan about life. <br /><br />And while psychic cats don't do it for my in the cozy mystery genre, I could get behind a psychic cat in a fantasy book maybe.<br /><br />Anyway, not my cup of tea. But it is about the length of an Agatha Christie mystery and those ARE my cup of tea. They just happen to be a little less cutesy and a little more dramatic. All the drama here takes place off the page and is recounted later. Even when people are dying it's all very "Oh dear, well I guess we'll have to do something else today since our boat has exploded killing the driver." </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11757478618281952515">...more</a>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8252740531852955898">People who flock to Mackinac Island and enjoy mysteries will enjoy this tome. Though named differently, the mysteries take place on Breakfast (or Pear, or Grand, or Pirate, or ....) Island. The name changes depending on the type of resident. There are a lot of similarities between this fictitious island and Mackinac Island.<br /><br />Fellow "The Cat Who..." fans already know the main characters and what they are usually up to. If you've been paying attention, Qwill and the siamese reside in a different place in each book.<br /><br />I'm leaving out my synopsis, because that has always been the same. However, these stories are NEVER boring. I'm having a fun time with Qwill, Koko and Yum Yum!<br /><br />Once again, if you love Mackinac Island, Michigan, and mystery, you'll love this!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4645017527129792075">Not thrilled about this one. It seemed like they put the majority of the mystery solving in the last two chapters of the book and the rest of the chapters galavanting around breakfast island. However, the book did have potential, and since it was my first cat who book I'd be willing to give the series another shot before I doom them to the will not read shelf</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1279988999?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 25, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3263613-michelle" class="user" title="Michelle">Michelle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3263613-michelle?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1279988999">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8345570932732713425">I continue to be impressed by the late author's mastery of language. Reading her books on Kindle expands my vocabulary, which is great fun.<br /><br />As for the book, I'm really tired of Qwill and his curmudgeonly benevolence. He seemed less dimensional in this book than in the previous books. During the series, he's gone from being a somewhat realistic character to a "wise, knowing, curmudgeon who gives his billions to the community." <br /><br />In this book, there seems to have been less emphasis and development on</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8345570932732713425">I continue to be impressed by the late author's mastery of language. Reading her books on Kindle expands my vocabulary, which is great fun.<br /><br />As for the book, I'm really tired of Qwill and his curmudgeonly benevolence. He seemed less dimensional in this book than in the previous books. During the series, he's gone from being a somewhat realistic character to a "wise, knowing, curmudgeon who gives his billions to the community." <br /><br />In this book, there seems to have been less emphasis and development on reoccurring characters, compared to previous ones. We meet Lori and Nick's kids, but nothing new about their characters. I've always enjoyed Lori's connections to the cats, and that was barely touched on here. <br /><br />New characters are introduced, so it will be interesting to see how the young, timid, but intelligent "Liz" will play out.<br /><br />This story line with Polly is old. Having Polly jealous of "younger and thinner women" is old<br /><br />The cats helping to solve clues wasn't as clear as in the past.<br /><br />It was less enjoyable than some of the other books in this series. <br /><br />It will be interesting to see where the next ones goes.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16381164462870292460">Bon, vous l’avez sans doute compris avec toutes les critiques que j’ai déjà pu poster sur la série des « Le chat qui… », j’adore ces livres ! Encore une fois, c’est avec joie que j’ai pu retrouver les différents personnages.<br />Cette histoire se passe sur une île, ça change un peu de d’habitude et c’est pas plus mal.<br />Les mystères qui entourent cette fameuse île m’ont tenu en halène de bout en bout et je me demandais vraiment comment cela pourrait finir.<br />Parfois, je me dis que les histoires de ce journ</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16381164462870292460">Bon, vous l’avez sans doute compris avec toutes les critiques que j’ai déjà pu poster sur la série des « Le chat qui… », j’adore ces livres ! Encore une fois, c’est avec joie que j’ai pu retrouver les différents personnages.<br />Cette histoire se passe sur une île, ça change un peu de d’habitude et c’est pas plus mal.<br />Les mystères qui entourent cette fameuse île m’ont tenu en halène de bout en bout et je me demandais vraiment comment cela pourrait finir.<br />Parfois, je me dis que les histoires de ce journaliste qui résout les énigmes en parlant à ses chats sont un peu des romans pour enfants mais étant donné qu’il y a souvent des histoires de meurtres, ce n’est quand même pas le cas. Ce côté livre pour enfant qui n’en est pas a vraiment son charme et c’est ce que j’apprécie dans cette série.<br />Par contre, il faudrait vraiment que je lise les livres dans l’ordre car je me spoile involontairement certains passages de l’histoire de fond de la vie de Qwill.<br />En bref : un livre à lire, comme tous les autres !</span>

      <a href="/user/show/3668071-lisa-kucharski" class="user" title="Lisa Kucharski">Lisa Kucharski</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer831694071">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16457355418383730810">I love the characters in this series which kept me reading this story, however the mystery was so distant... and Qwill's ability to get information so elusive that the quick summation at the end fell flat for me. In this story, Qwill goes to a nearby island where a new summer resort has pretty much inflicted itself and its crass commercialism on the locals. He goes to investigate a series of "accidents" and ends up trying to investigate but ... I it felt more like he was just wandering about. <br /><br />Br</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16457355418383730810">I love the characters in this series which kept me reading this story, however the mystery was so distant... and Qwill's ability to get information so elusive that the quick summation at the end fell flat for me. In this story, Qwill goes to a nearby island where a new summer resort has pretty much inflicted itself and its crass commercialism on the locals. He goes to investigate a series of "accidents" and ends up trying to investigate but ... I it felt more like he was just wandering about. <br /><br />Braun has a certain formula that one can feel in her stories and in this one it doesn't gel soon enough to get the story some momentum. If you are considering skipping one of these stories... this would be one to skip.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13389947458285334172">This is one of my favorite books in the series...A series that, though I know I shouldn't, I unashamedly love. The characters are so cute and endearing that I find myself absorbed the instant I open the book. It brings back good feels as the small towns and bee-in-the-bonnet, meddling, yet well-meaning personalities of the inhabitants remind me of the one I grew up in, and I find Braun's writing is charming as can be. Though they are usually pretty predictable, I read for the characters and thei</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13389947458285334172">This is one of my favorite books in the series...A series that, though I know I shouldn't, I unashamedly love. The characters are so cute and endearing that I find myself absorbed the instant I open the book. It brings back good feels as the small towns and bee-in-the-bonnet, meddling, yet well-meaning personalities of the inhabitants remind me of the one I grew up in, and I find Braun's writing is charming as can be. Though they are usually pretty predictable, I read for the characters and their surroundings, more than for the mystery. I positively adore Jim Qwilleran, his mustache, his cats, and his gruff, yet kind manner. This is the series I find myself reaching for between those long, hard reads where I just need to relax and be lost in something fun and light.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer259232951">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5690258512950335735">This is one of two books out of the entire series that I have never read, due to the completely futile search to find them. Then, unexpectedly, my sister gave me a gift voucher for my birthday to Dymock's. I assumed the stores I visited in bigger cities would still be open, but the recent closures meant it was impossible to find one, so after a few months deliberation, I went online and to order books.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText5690258512950335735">This is one of two books out of the entire series that I have never read, due to the completely futile search to find them. Then, unexpectedly, my sister gave me a gift voucher for my birthday to Dymock's. I assumed the stores I visited in bigger cities would still be open, but the recent closures meant it was impossible to find one, so after a few months deliberation, I went online and to order books. I didn't expect there to be any available, but after typing in 'Lilian Jackson Braun' it came up with a few select titles...and the two I wanted were on the list! The delivery was prompt and the service was one of the best I've had ordering online.<br /><br />On to the book. I think I enjoyed this one more than most of the titles, which is hard because I love this series. This one had all the elements I love, and Koko's clues were just as devious as ever. Polly of course, being out of the scene, is definitely a plus point. The change of setting, but still with the usual Pickaxe characters made for interesting reading, especially Lori and Nick, two of my favorite characters. Even Dwight and Andy make appearances, and Arch is his usual comical self. The knowledge now, that I only have one book out of this entire series I've never read before is actually kind of depressing, but I'm going to move onto the Cat who knew a cardinal soon<br /><br />If you love a cozy mystery, or even if you just love cats and descriptions of delicious food then these books are for you!</span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2450318.The_Cat_Who_Came_to_Breakfast" title="Audio CD 9781590074855" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=myst-cosies" class="actionLinkLite">myst-cosies</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=myst-set-andor-auth-usa" class="actionLinkLite">myst-set-andor-auth-usa</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer270825889">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14845998991073810224">BOTTOM LINE: This 16th in the long series has Qwilleran visiting his friends The Bambas, on Breakfast Island, a newly developed formerly "hunting lodges only" little place in the a lake near Pickaxe. A good, solidly satisfying cosy, with strong characters and a fast-moving plot. <br /><br />A couple of weeks vacation starts out interesting and winds up deadly, as Qwill heads for the highly promoted “Pear Island Resorts”, a new development near which the Bambas are fixing up their bed’n’breakfast. Suspicious</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14845998991073810224">BOTTOM LINE: This 16th in the long series has Qwilleran visiting his friends The Bambas, on Breakfast Island, a newly developed formerly "hunting lodges only" little place in the a lake near Pickaxe. A good, solidly satisfying cosy, with strong characters and a fast-moving plot. <br /><br />A couple of weeks vacation starts out interesting and winds up deadly, as Qwill heads for the highly promoted “Pear Island Resorts”, a new development near which the Bambas are fixing up their bed’n’breakfast. Suspicious events abound, as the islanders don’t seem to appreciate all the modcons the developers have brought with them, and people start dying nastily. Wonderful setting, a grand finale with a hurricane, Nick and Laurie’s family, and some island “characters” make this an entertaining tale. Although there’s a touch too much woowoo and coincidence regarding KoKo for my liking, the plotting is solid. This one was lots of fun, and Guidall's narration was, as always, perfectly done.<br /></span>

          </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer511875254">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer179243268101531536">This book was not as good (to me) as the previous Cat Who books. For one thing, Qwil didn't seem quite like himself and the early chapters. For the entire first half of the book it seemed like little to nothing was going on, except for Quil's meandering around Breakfast Island, being a crotchety old man, not even taking his usual interest in people or paying much attention to the cats.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText179243268101531536">This book was not as good (to me) as the previous Cat Who books. For one thing, Qwil didn't seem quite like himself and the early chapters. For the entire first half of the book it seemed like little to nothing was going on, except for Quil's meandering around Breakfast Island, being a crotchety old man, not even taking his usual interest in people or paying much attention to the cats. I give it a 3 star rating because the book comes through in the last several chapters -- Qwill is more like himself, Koko's brilliance again shines through and the surprise as far as 'who done it' and who was who and who was related to who was a good one.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer359194574">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2034786180857057576">I listened to this book, which I have read before. I was watching an interview by the creator, actors, and writers of White Collar, a TV show. The creator of the show described it as a "Blue Sky" show, or a show that leaves people feeling good. That is the way I feel about The Cat Who books. I enjoy visiting the characters in the books, and I enjoy the cats. There are crimes and murders, but they aren't the main focus of the books. There are friendships, and various interactions of the people in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2034786180857057576">I listened to this book, which I have read before. I was watching an interview by the creator, actors, and writers of White Collar, a TV show. The creator of the show described it as a "Blue Sky" show, or a show that leaves people feeling good. That is the way I feel about The Cat Who books. I enjoy visiting the characters in the books, and I enjoy the cats. There are crimes and murders, but they aren't the main focus of the books. There are friendships, and various interactions of the people in the stories. </span>

      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sckV1ofuWuntcgD+99IqkclMNyotzfKZoX9tZy1XRivUHSoFdTxOE2GqdEWJs8wjgLv0M2QQtTPLdmj14cKwbg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CDbtkCAVqW8+LHfDeYncGVdu0maSgmMbua3RPeFW2eRt4tJD0se9lbL0A3gH6DqrHpkRf9tfJLHTpNSvLcMvoQ==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/21625.Lilian_Jackson_Braun">About Lilian Jackson Braun</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/21625.Lilian_Jackson_Braun"><img alt="21625" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1206733773p2/21625.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer4295560076371444662">Lilian Jackson Braun was an American writer. She is well-known for her light-hearted series of <em>The Cat Who...</em> mystery novels. The <em>Cat Who</em> books center around the life of former newspaper reporter James Qwilleran, and his two Siamese cats, KoKo and Yum Yum in the fictitious small town of Pickax located in Moose County, "400 miles north of everywhere." Although never formally stated in the books, th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4295560076371444662">Lilian Jackson Braun was an American writer. She is well-known for her light-hearted series of <em>The Cat Who...</em> mystery novels. The <em>Cat Who</em> books center around the life of former newspaper reporter James Qwilleran, and his two Siamese cats, KoKo and Yum Yum in the fictitious small town of Pickax located in Moose County, "400 miles north of everywhere." Although never formally stated in the books, the towns, counties and lifestyles described in the series are generally accepted to be a modeled after Bad Axe, Michigan (located in the "Michigan Thumb") where she resided with her husband for many years until the mid 1980's. Many also believe that the culture and history of the Upper peninsula of Michigan are represented in the series as well, which is quite possible as it is indeed a fictitious location.<br /><br />Lilian Jackson Braun began her writing career as a teenager, contributing sports poetry for the <em>Detroit News</em>. She later began working as an advertising copywriter for many of Detroit's department stores. After that stint, she worked at the Detroit Free Press as the "Good Living" editor for 30 years. She retired from the Free Press in 1978.<br /><br />Between 1966 and 1968, she published three novels to critical acclaim: <em>The Cat Who Could Read Backwards, The Cat Who Ate Danish Modern</em> and <em>The Cat Who Turned On and Off</em>. In 1966, <em>The New York Times</em> labeled Braun, "the new detective of the year." The rising mystery author disappeared from the publishing scene for 18 years. The blame came from the fact that mystery novels were starting to focus on sex, violence, and foul language, and Braun's light-hearted books were not welcome in this new territory. It wasn't until 1986 that the Berkley Publishing Group reintroduced Braun to the public with the publication of an original paperback, <em>The Cat Who Saw Red</em>. Within two years, Berkeley released four new novels in paperback and reprinted the three mysteries from the sixties. Braun's series became an instant best seller once again. In January 2007 the twenty-ninth novel in the series, <em>The Cat Who Had 60 Whiskers</em>, was released in hardcover by the Penguin Group.<br /><br />Not much was really known about Braun, as she prefered to keep her private life that way. For years, publishers have given inaccurate accounts of her year of birth, which has remained unknown until she openly acknowledged her age in an interview for the Detroit News in January 2005.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4295560076371444662">...more</a>

    </div>
